    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3077066997468100303">"A publisher in New York asked me to write down what I know about the Greek gods, and I was like, Can we do this anonymously? Because I don't need the Olympians mad at me again. But if it helps you to know your Greek gods, and survive an encounter with them if they ever show up in your face, then I guess writing all this down will be my good deed for the week." So begins P</span>
  <span id="freeText3077066997468100303" style="display:none">"A publisher in New York asked me to write down what I know about the Greek gods, and I was like, Can we do this anonymously? Because I don't need the Olympians mad at me again. But if it helps you to know your Greek gods, and survive an encounter with them if they ever show up in your face, then I guess writing all this down will be my good deed for the week." So begins Percy Jackson's Greek Gods, in which the son of Poseidon adds his own magic--and sarcastic asides--to the classics. He explains how the world was created, then gives readers his personal take on a who's who of ancients, from Apollo to Zeus. Percy does not hold back. "If you like horror shows, blood baths, lying, stealing, backstabbing, and cannibalism, then read on, because it definitely was a Golden Age for all that." Dramatic full-color illustrations throughout by Caldecott Honoree John Rocco make this volume--a must for home, library, and classroom shelves--as stunning as it is entertaining.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3077066997468100303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_743975881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743975881" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743975881?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june">pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=laugh-out-loud-humor">laugh-out-loud-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fabulous-five-stars">fabulous-five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=greek-mythology">greek-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743975881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3452408401119750402"><b>4.5 stars<br/><br/>Reasons to read Percy Jackson's Greek Gods to your kids (or let them read on their own without any parental censoring):<br/><br/>1. R-rated action</b><br/><br/>There's rape—in so many forms! Zeus ravaging Demeter as a cobra, Poseidon ravaging Demeter as a horse, Hades kidnapping Demeter...'s daughter, Persephone to be his wife and play footies with under the covers. Actually, throw zoophilia in there too.<br/><br/>And incest! Zeus married his sister, Hera; Hades married his niece; Poseiden bumped uglies with his sister.</span>
  <span id="freeText3452408401119750402" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars<br><br>Reasons to read Percy Jackson's Greek Gods to your kids (or let them read on their own without any parental censoring):<br><br>1. R-rated action</b><br><br>There's rape—in so many forms! Zeus ravaging Demeter as a cobra, Poseidon ravaging Demeter as a horse, Hades kidnapping Demeter...'s daughter, Persephone to be his wife and play footies with under the covers. Actually, throw zoophilia in there too.<br><br>And incest! Zeus married his sister, Hera; Hades married his niece; Poseiden bumped uglies with his sister... the gods make Game of Throne look tame.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410420265ra/11105343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's also cannibalism, murder, thievery... if that doesn't make you the favorite parent, I don't know what will.<br><br><b>2. It's family-friendly</b><br><br>It is middle-grade after all and Riordan does a fantastic job of covering up some of the, ahem, nastier bits. The word 'rape' is only ever mentioned once and is used in context of a mortal. When the gods do it, it's delicately written as "so-and-so got his way" or "so-and-so got a little too cuddly with the unfortunate other so-and-so". <br><br>The incest is bluntly mentioned, but Percy spins it by saying the gods don't view relationships the same way humans do, which is valid. Hell, they're gods, they can do whatever or <i>who</i>ever they want.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410420080ra/11105321.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>3. There are Public Service Announcements</b><br><br>In a book where no punishments are awarded to the main characters, that is, the gods, there has to be <i>some</i> preaching to mold the minds of the impressionable young who will, for once, be quiet while they devour the passages of Ouranus devouring his kids. There's the usual: no drinking until you're 30, don't have sex in temples, eating your kids will cause your wife to plot your demise, etc. <br><br>But what I love best is the overarching <b>feminist</b> themes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410420080ra/11105322.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With goddesses themselves being violated left and right, I think a little education would be beneficial. Percy also comments on how unfair it is that the goddesses weren't invited to the meeting to decide who rules over what. Veterans of the Percy Jackson series already know that Riordan is capable of creating strong, intelligent female characters and equally as strong and intelligent male characters who don't necessarily feel the need to remind everyone of his masculinity or top his female companions. Percy is a fantastic example of the latter:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Back in the old days, the writers (who were all guys) would say, "See? This story shows you that women are troublemakers! It's all their fault!"<br>Epimetheus and Pandora. Adam and Eve. The blame game has been going on for a long time.<br> <br>Zeus got his way. Afterward, Kallisto was too ashamed to say anything. She was afraid it was somehow her fault. Pro tip: if you're attacked by a creep, it's never your fault. Tell somebody. </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410420080ra/11105323.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>4. It's hilarious </b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I am king of the universe!" [Ouranus/Sky] bellowed. "How could I not be? I am literally above everything else."<br><br>“He was also the god of (take a deep breath) commerce, languages, thievery, cheeseburgers, trickery, eloquent speaking, feasts, cheeseburgers, hospitality, guard dogs, birds of omen, gymnastics, athletic competitions, cheeseburgers, cheeseburgers and telling fortunes with dice. Okay, I just tossed in the cheeseburgers to see if you were paying attention. Also, I’m hungry.”<br><br>“I mean, five gods in one stomach—dang. That's enough for doubles tennis, including a ref. They'd been down there so long, they were probably hoping Kronos would swallow down a deck of cards or a Monopoly game.” <br><br></i>
</blockquote><br>Need I go on?<br><br><b>5. Percy's narrating</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Some girls might've asked for front-row tickets to the hottest boy band concert, or a date with someone awesome, like, I don't know, Percy Jackson, or somebody. (What—it could happen)</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Yes, that's a reason. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398765040ra/9460927.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you're a beginner at Greek mythology or eager to become someone's favorite aunt/uncle (and get crossed off their parents' Christmas card list), give Percy Jackson's Greek Gods a try. The sole reason I knocked off 0.5 star was because I'd read all these myths before in their true, uncensored glory as a child(insert image of nine-year-old me grinning as Kronos chopped his dad's balls off), and even Percy's special brand of snark couldn't put a new enough spin on them to fully earn my interest. But for you, my dear untainted soul, prepare to have your mind blown.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/491396.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3452408401119750402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756572551" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5169771298326905110">I love Rick Riordan; he just has a gift that anything he writes is very readable. I liked this book, as well.<br/><br/>However, I do have pretty good knowledge of Greek mythology; I sometimes found this slightly dull. Still, it got the Percy Jackson vibes to the writing and everything. So, I would say that overall, this is 3 and a half stars for me. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer17851830609468910344"><i>Teacher: Does anyone know something about Greek Mythology?<br/>Me (after reading Percy Jackson's book): </i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469555504ra/19830854.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>I wrote it many times, but one more time: You don't find better book about Greek Mythology than those from Rick Riordan. He should definitely write all text books, because he would turn studying in something you will enjoy. In this book you get to know main Greek Gods in a hilarious way, which can provide only Rick's writing style. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>She (Tethys) ended up marrying Oceanus, which was kind of a no-</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17851830609468910344" style="display:none"><i>Teacher: Does anyone know something about Greek Mythology?<br>Me (after reading Percy Jackson's book): </i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469555504ra/19830854.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I wrote it many times, but one more time: You don't find better book about Greek Mythology than those from Rick Riordan. He should definitely write all text books, because he would turn studying in something you will enjoy. In this book you get to know main Greek Gods in a hilarious way, which can provide only Rick's writing style. <br><br><b>
  <i>She (Tethys) ended up marrying Oceanus, which was kind of a no-brainer. 'Hey, you like water? I like water too! We should totally go out!'</i>
</b><br><br>My personal favorite narration was suprisingly about Hades and Hephaestus, not my favorite Apollo. That one was actually the most boring.<br><br><b>
  <i>Hera pushed her bowl away. 'And where is your son Pelops?'<br>'Actually,' Tantalus said, 'that's him in the stew. Suprise, you idiots! Ha, ha! Ha, ha!'<br>Honestly, I don't know what he was expecting. Did he think the gods would chuckle and slap him on the back? Oh, Tantalus, you old kidder, Good one'</i>
</b><br><br>I didn't want to read it at first. I thought it will be another boring book about Mythology, but <u>no</u>.<br><b>I enjoyed every chapter, every page!</b> <br>If you are in a bad mood, read it. It surely cheer you up. I highly recommend it and I swear it's not waste of time and you will not regret. </span>

<div id="review_733113145" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/733113145" />
    <a title="Neha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11946600-neha"><img alt="Neha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485571919p2/11946600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/733113145?book_show_action=true">Oct 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neha" href="/user/show/11946600-neha">Neha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer733113145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8399398064484824307"><b>
  <u> Pre-Reading Review: </u>
</b> (Real Review included below :D)<br/>Do I really need to elaborate how this book will deserve more than 5 stars? Because being a Percy Jackson and basically a Rick Riordan fan, we 'know' how awesome this book is gonna be. But if you really wanna know why, here are some reasons-<br/>1.<i> Book Cover</i>- FANTABULOUS COVER! Seriously, The cover says all! How can you not just get the urge to peek inside a little after seeing the cover of this book? <br/><br/>2.<i> Percy's POV </i>- Percy Jackson, who being </span>
  <span id="freeText8399398064484824307" style="display:none"><b>
  <u> Pre-Reading Review: </u>
</b> (Real Review included below :D)<br />Do I really need to elaborate how this book will deserve more than 5 stars? Because being a Percy Jackson and basically a Rick Riordan fan, we 'know' how awesome this book is gonna be. But if you really wanna know why, here are some reasons-<br />1.<i> Book Cover</i>- FANTABULOUS COVER! Seriously, The cover says all! How can you not just get the urge to peek inside a little after seeing the cover of this book? <br /><br />2.<i> Percy's POV </i>- Percy Jackson, who being a modern world teenager, has a sarcastic yet easily descriptive point of view, with scenes so well elaborated that even a five year old child can imagine them well. Plus his witty comments win the hearts of millions of his fans!<br /><br />3.<i> Greek Mythologies </i>- Greek Mythologies, without a doubt, are one of the most famous mythologies. Honestly, I didn't know much about Greek Mythology (an understatement really :P) before reading Percy Jackson &amp; Olympian Series. So, I'd love to know more!<br /><br />Waiting for the book eagerly!!!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u> Real Review or Post-Reading Review</u>
</b><br /><br />What did I tell you??? *virtually elbowing you right now* You're welcome By the way :D!<br /><br />Alrighty, SO This book has Just officially BLOWN my mind. I mean, come on, could this book be more Awesome than that, in any freaking way?? This was the <u>HEIGHT of EPICNESS!</u><br /><br />This book gave me EVERYTHING I hoped for and SO MUCH MORE! I craved for Knowledge- I got so much of it I think my head is going to explode (nah, not really, but you know what I mean.) I craved for Percy's sassiness- we get to enjoy that so much that I still can't contain my smile whenever I remember a quote from this book. I desperately wanted to see the illustrations- and they were just Marvelous. <br /><br />The most important part is that we get to actually observe the Greek Gods in their days. Before this book, whenever I read Heroes of Olympus series and the Demigods would say that Gods are so dangerous and stuff, I would be like <i> Psshh...</i> They're okay! They're not that scary as demigods think. But now...uh, not so much. If I was a demigod, or even a mortal that somehow got involved in the world of Gods, I would be pretty much running away from them, because they're DANGEROUS! I mean, seriously, no wonder Demigod life is hard!<br /><br />Some stories were so intriguing, like Athena's. Some were a bit emotional, like Hephaestus and even Dionysus (the wine dude!). And yeah, some were pretty gross too; but thanks to Uncle Rick they were actually pretty funny to hear (but no, I'd rather not see those incidents in real life). And some of them were soooo sweet, like the Hades and Persephone love story (I did some countless 'Awwwwws' during that). All in all, this WHOLE book, Was a bucket full of <b>AWESOME!</b><br /><br />So, once again, Thankyou so so so much Percy Jackson for writing this one (of course <i>he</i> gets the credit, right?). I bet there must be many difficulties, which most likely includes Gods and Monsters, but just keep being Awesome like that! And if possible, write more. <br /><br /><i>Olympians Rulez</i><br /><br /><u>P.S.- Psst, Uncle Rick, how about Jason Grace's Roman Gods? *wink wink*</u></span>
  <a data-text-id="8399398064484824307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3862660946801417845">I was first introduced to Percy Jackson over eight years ago and my love for this series and Rick Riordan has only grown over the years. When Rick Riordan announced that these books were finally getting their own series, I sobbed and jumped in joy. These books and these characters mean so much to me!! <br/><br/>I was determined to reread the entire series but a few moments later, the idea seemed slightly daunting. And then my gaze landed on this book in my bookshelf and I realized that even though I'd bou</span>
  <span id="freeText3862660946801417845" style="display:none">I was first introduced to Percy Jackson over eight years ago and my love for this series and Rick Riordan has only grown over the years. When Rick Riordan announced that these books were finally getting their own series, I sobbed and jumped in joy. These books and these characters mean so much to me!! <br /><br />I was determined to reread the entire series but a few moments later, the idea seemed slightly daunting. And then my gaze landed on this book in my bookshelf and I realized that even though I'd bought it six years ago, for some reason I never got around to reading it. <br /><br />And so I finally read it and loved it and felt like I was thirteen again, engrossed in the world of Greek Gods and the shitstorm they always seem to be brewing. Greek mythology narrated by Percy Jackson is the only way I want to learn about the subject. No one can do it better. <br /><br />So, obviously, it deserves all the stars!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14615288662857164617">Oh, so much fun. <br/><br/>I am an ardent <b>PERCY JACKSON</b> fan. And I don't care if <b>Rick Riordan</b> is milking a cash cow here by spinning out...er....spinoffs. <br/><br/>I <i>will</i> read them all.<br/><br/>Percy Jackson telling the tale of the Greek Gods, or to be more precise, his sincerely powerful and definitely dysfunctional family is pure gold. In vintage Seaweed-Brain style, the treatement of the Gods is irreverent, bordering on cheeky and utterly lacking in blind adulation. Percy tells it like it is. <br/><br/>From <b>Gaia</b> who probably inve</span>
  <span id="freeText14615288662857164617" style="display:none">Oh, so much fun. <br><br>I am an ardent <b>PERCY JACKSON</b> fan. And I don't care if <b>Rick Riordan</b> is milking a cash cow here by spinning out...er....spinoffs. <br><br>I <i>will</i> read them all.<br><br>Percy Jackson telling the tale of the Greek Gods, or to be more precise, his sincerely powerful and definitely dysfunctional family is pure gold. In vintage Seaweed-Brain style, the treatement of the Gods is irreverent, bordering on cheeky and utterly lacking in blind adulation. Percy tells it like it is. <br><br>From <b>Gaia</b> who probably invented the first swear words to the gentleness and wisdom of <b>Hestia</b> to <b>Demeter</b> going grainzilla on amorous men to <b>Hera</b> being Hera (with a dash of jealousy and revenge and scary punishments) to <b>Hades</b> channelling his inner Japanese Manga Emo to <b>Poseidon</b> being a likeable bloke with quite a few barnacles in his closet to <b>Athena</b> being wise but prone to professional rivalry to <b>Aphrodite</b> being the Olympian version of high-school MEAN GIRL - LEVEL 1 to <b>Ares</b> and his nucleur bursts of passion and cowardice and adultery to <b>Hephaestus</b> and his mother-issues to <i>hand-me-a-pair-shades-he-shines-so-bright</i> haiku spouting <b>Apollo</b> to <b>Artemis</b> who had her priorities in place (stalkery creeping men, notwithstanding) to <b>Hermes</b> who spent his first day being born by stealing cows and chomping them down wih Steak sauce to <b>Dionysus</b> who invented the very first wine press to the grand poobah himself, <b>Zeus</b> (or as Percy's refers to him....ol'ThunderPants) and his many MANY affairs; <br><br>Percy spills all.<br><br>I was snorting gleefully over lines like:<br><br><b>
  <i>"His big claim to fame was that the Golden Fleece - that magical sheepskin rug I'm related to - ended up in his kingdom, which made the place immune to disease, invasion, stock-market crashes, visits from Justin Beiber and pretty much any other natural disaster."</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408509923ra/10858007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A must-have for all Percy Jackson fans and a fun introduction into the world of Greek Gods.<br><br><br>(<i>And oh!....it had a tiny *WHEN Percy Jackson MET Carter Kane* short story at the end. Which was rather endearing. And definitely grist for the Riordan myth factory</i>)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1032291420?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Cook" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Cook" href="/user/show/17753712-hannah-cook">Hannah Cook</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032291420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2584170025252642594">This is easily the best book of Greek myths ever! It was interesting, I learned a lot, and best of all, it was narrated by PERCY. FREAKING. JACKSON! All the sass we know and love was back and better than ever! Also, THE FUNNY CHAPTER TITLES YESSSS! Words can't describe how much I miss the chapter titles in the Heroes of Olympus! <br/>All the stories in this book were so well put together, which in itself was great, but they were so funny! It's rare I didn't grin really big at least a few times a chap</span>
  <span id="freeText2584170025252642594" style="display:none">This is easily the best book of Greek myths ever! It was interesting, I learned a lot, and best of all, it was narrated by PERCY. FREAKING. JACKSON! All the sass we know and love was back and better than ever! Also, THE FUNNY CHAPTER TITLES YESSSS! Words can't describe how much I miss the chapter titles in the Heroes of Olympus! <br />All the stories in this book were so well put together, which in itself was great, but they were so funny! It's rare I didn't grin really big at least a few times a chapter. I mean come on, gems like these are what make life worth living. Let me put down some good ones:<br />"A mass-murdering psychopath who plays the lyre? It doesn't get more charming than that!"<br />You can't swing a cat in Ancient Greece without hitting one of Zeus's ex-girlfriends."<br />"If you plan on living forever by sticking the god of death under your bed, you're out of luck."<br />And the chapter titles! "Demeter turns into Granzilla" Zeus kills everyone" "Ares, the manly man's manly man." "Apollo sings and dances and shoots people" SO MUCH GREATNESS. SO MUCH!<br />This book was so fun to read, and tided me over for a couple days during he AGONIZING WAIT for The Blood of Olympus. Definitely pick up this book, if only for Persassy's sassy sass! Good luck in the rest of the wait for BOO, fellow Demigods!</span>

<div id="review_1972632189" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1972632189" />
    <a title="Cris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63364301-cris"><img alt="Cris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605625049p2/63364301.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1972632189?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cris" href="/user/show/63364301-cris">Cris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63364301-cris?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63364301-cris?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63364301-cris?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63364301-cris?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1972632189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4115772727282485944"><b>English/Italiano</b><br/><p>First of all, I have to say I am not a native english speaker so, please, I prefer to not be attacked, if I made any mistakes. Instead of do that, it would be nice if you corrected me, thank you :)</p><br/><p>I wrote this review <i>ages</i> ago, but I’m posting it just now because I wrote it in a piece of paper and I, uhm, am a <i>lazy</i> person so I left the review in paper instead of writing it on computer. The reason why I didn’t write it in computer at first is because it got broken (it still is and </p></span>
  <span id="freeText4115772727282485944" style="display:none"><b>English/Italiano</b><br /><p>First of all, I have to say I am not a native english speaker so, please, I prefer to not be attacked, if I made any mistakes. Instead of do that, it would be nice if you corrected me, thank you :)</p><br /><p>I wrote this review <i>ages</i> ago, but I’m posting it just now because I wrote it in a piece of paper and I, uhm, am a <i>lazy</i> person so I left the review in paper instead of writing it on computer. The reason why I didn’t write it in computer at first is because it got broken (it still is and I don’t think there is a coming back). I got my dad’s computer, but it is not like mine <i>*insert sad face here*</i></p><br /><p>Anyways, let’s get into the real mini review. <b>This book is a companion book</b>, an adding book to the Percy Jackson and the Olympians series. I recommend reading it, <i> only</i> after finishing the series because there are some little spoilers. <b>Novellas and adding books are sometimes ignored and not read. I personally think this is a good one that has to be read</b>, it doesn’t add anything to the story, but it will help you to understand more greek gods and you will know something more about greek mythology (which <i>isn’t that bad</i>, you know).</p><br /><p><b>• It’s greek mythology and Rick Riordan so it’s interesting and funny at the same time! </b> You want any help to study mythology but you want it to be entertainment as well? This book is the perfect solution for you! <s>(I swear this isn’t a commercial)</s>. <b>Rick Riordan’s style is simple, hilarious</b> and he tried to put all the versions of the myths together. This cannot be ignored: telling greek mythology isn’t easy, there are a lot of versions out there of a single myth and Rick Riordan did his researches so well. Not everyone could make it. For example, I couldn’t at all!</p><br /><p><b>•</b> <b>It’s told by Percy Jackson!</b> Exactly, our favourite demigod tell us everything, starting from the beggining . He tries not to add a lot of persional opinions, but of course <b>the result is a mix of funny jokes plus interesting facts. </b></p><br /><p>•  <b>If you are thinking, greek mythology = heavy and hard book to read, then you are completely wrong</b>. It’s the perfect “I want to read something light, but also want to feel more intelligent after it and not want to be discriminated by the fact not all readers do read 500 pages books AND don’t want to read a contemporary because most of light reads are c-o-n-t-e-m-p-o-r-a-r-i-e-s”. Don’t start writing insulting comments, I <i>do</i> love contemporaries, but let’s face it.</p><br /><p>I didn’t rate it 5 stars because I don’t think it is a 5 star read. Still awesome, though.</p><br /><br /><p><b>Italiano</b><br />Ho scritto questa recensione <i>molto</i> tempo fa, ma la sto postando solo adesso perché l’avevo scritta su un foglio di carta e io, uhm, sono una persona <i>pigra</i> quindi ho lasciato la recensione sul pezzo di carta invece che scriverla sul computer. La ragione per cui non l’ho scritta sul computer dall’inizio è perché si era rotto (lo è ancora e non credo che si possa riparare). Ho preso il computer di mio padre, ma non è come il mio <i>*inserire faccina triste qui*</i></p><br /><p>Comunque, andiamo direttamente alla mini-recensione. <b>Questo libro è un companion </b>, un libro aggiuntivo alla saga di Percy Jackson e Gli Dei Dell’Olimpo. Ne consiglio la lettura, <i> solo</i> dopo aver finito la lettura della saga perché ci sono dei piccoli spoiler. <b>Novelle e libri aggiuntivi sono a volte ignorati e non letti. Personalmente io penso che questo sia uno buono che deve essere letto </b>, non aggiunge niente alla storia, ma ti aiuterà a capire di più gli dei greci e saprai qualcosa in più sulla mitologia greca (che <i>non è così male</i>, sai).</p><br /><p><b>• È mitologia greca e Rick Riordan quindi è interessante e divertente allo stesso tempo! </b> Vuoi un aiuto per studiare mitologia ma vuoi essere anche intrattenuto? Questo libro è perfetto per te! <s>(giuro che non è una pubblicità)</s>. <b>Lo stile di Rick Riordan è semplice, esilarante</b> e ha provato a mettere tutte le versioni dei miti insieme. Ciò non può essere ignorato: raccontare la mitologia greca non è facile, la fuori ci sono tantissime versione di un solo mito e Rick Riordan ha condotto le sue ricerche così bene. Non tutti ce la farebbero. Per esempio, io per niente!</p><br /><p><b>•</b> <b>È raccontato da Percy Jackson!</b> Esattamente, il nostro semidio preferito ci racconta tutto, cominciando dall’inizio. Cerca di non aggiungere molte opinioni personali, ma naturalmente <b>il risultato è misto di battute divertenti con fatti interessanti. </b></p><br /><p>•  <b>Se stai pensando, mitologia greca = pesante e difficile libro da leggere, allora hai completamente sbagliato</b>. È il perfetto “Voglio qualcosa di leggero, ma anche sentirmi più intelligente dopo e non voglio essere discriminato perché non tutti i lettori leggono libri con 500 pagine E non voglio leggere un contemporaneo adesso perché la maggior parte delle letture leggere sono c-o-n-t-e-m-p-o-r-a-n-e-i”. Non iniziate a scrivere commenti dove mi insultate, mi piacciono <i>davvero tanto</i> i contemporanei, ma ammettiamolo.</p><br /><p>Non gli ho dato 5 stelline perché non credo sia un libro da 5 stelline. Però è lo stesso fantastico.</p><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4115772727282485944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_749503750" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16529168-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485395880p2/16529168.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095247756?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/22888006-percy-jackson-and-the-greek-gods">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095247756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5140311914368306828">I've read all the Percy Jackson books, and the Heroes of Olympus series, so thought I'd enjoy this. I did. <br/><br/>Rick Riordan took on a mammoth task in compiling this book, with so many myths and legends surrounding Greek mythology. This is a great introduction to the twelve main Gods of Olympus for middle school children, with enough of the gore and violence left in to keep it interesting. By managing to stick solely to the main Gods, Riordan manages to keep the stories within the book on track, with</span>
  <span id="freeText5140311914368306828" style="display:none">I've read all the Percy Jackson books, and the Heroes of Olympus series, so thought I'd enjoy this. I did. <br /><br />Rick Riordan took on a mammoth task in compiling this book, with so many myths and legends surrounding Greek mythology. This is a great introduction to the twelve main Gods of Olympus for middle school children, with enough of the gore and violence left in to keep it interesting. By managing to stick solely to the main Gods, Riordan manages to keep the stories within the book on track, without getting bogged down by various side Gods, nymphs or hero quests. This allows the narrative to stick quite rigidly to a set pattern, which as a reader I certainly valued. I've read a fair few books now on Greek mythology, and although not the most comprehensive, this is certainly the most readable, and is easily accessible to readers on all levels. <br /><br />The only downside for me was Percy as the narrator. He's rather unreliable at times, and embellished some of the stories more than necessary. After a while this became a little tiresome. This might appeal more to a younger audience however. <br /><br />I understand that there's also a heroes book written in a similar vein, which I'll be sure to look into. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5140311914368306828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3512540635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer57075526496299674"><b>I wake up every morning and think: You know what would be good today? Not dying. </b><br/><br/><br/>I really liked this novella about the greek gods because i got to learn even more about then than i can in the main series and having Percy narrate this is even better. <br/><br/>One thing that i really enjoy about these books is how much history that Rick has gone through to make sure these are as accurate as they can possibly be for a middle grade series and it always makes these books more than just learning. Hestia, Demet</span>
  <span id="freeText57075526496299674" style="display:none"><b>I wake up every morning and think: You know what would be good today? Not dying. </b><br /><br /><br />I really liked this novella about the greek gods because i got to learn even more about then than i can in the main series and having Percy narrate this is even better. <br /><br />One thing that i really enjoy about these books is how much history that Rick has gone through to make sure these are as accurate as they can possibly be for a middle grade series and it always makes these books more than just learning. Hestia, Demeter, Persephone, Hera, Hades, Poseidon, Zeus, Athena, Aphrodite, Ares, Hephaestus, Apollo, Artemis, Hermes and Dionysus are the main focus in this book as there are way to many different gods to but into just one book so i'm glad it was just a selected few. <br /><br />My favourite three gods are Apollo, Artemis and Athena all for different reasons but my most favourite one out of them all would have to be Athena because she is just smart and knows how to be direct with everyone. <br /><br />I also enjoyed the little backstory each god got before there little adventure began and i can always count on Rick to make these stories more interesting rather than just spit out the facts of each god. <br /><br />Overall i really enjoyed this little extra bit of story and i would recommend this to any Percy Jackson fan who either wants more out of this story or just wants to learn about the greek gods. </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15725893-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562029499p2/15725893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1382647932?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/15725893-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15725893-anna?shelf=half-stars">half-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1382647932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3267100386403503360">By the gods, I missed Percy's narrative <b>so much</b> that starting this book I almost physically started hurting from the rainbows that developed in my tummy. I pretty much <u>loved</u> <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i>, but third POV just didn't suit Percy at all and I think he missed some of his magic that way.<br/><br/>Seriously, could you imagine this:<br/><blockquote>
  <i>"...First I'll tell you how the world got made. Then I'll run down a list of gods and give you my two cents about each of them. I just hope I don't make them so mad they inc</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3267100386403503360" style="display:none">By the gods, I missed Percy's narrative <b>so much</b> that starting this book I almost physically started hurting from the rainbows that developed in my tummy. I pretty much <u>loved</u> <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i>, but third POV just didn't suit Percy at all and I think he missed some of his magic that way.<br /><br />Seriously, could you imagine this:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"...First I'll tell you how the world got made. Then I'll run down a list of gods and give you my two cents about each of them. I just hope I don't make them so mad they incinerate me before I-</i>
  <br />
  <b>AGGHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!</b>
  <br />
  <i>Just kidding. Still here."</i>
</blockquote><br />...in 3rd person POV? It just doesn't fit.<br /><br />Now.<br /><br />About the book: It's in Percy's narrative. Need I say more?<br /><br />But seriously, if you read <i>The Heroes of Olympus</i> and <i>Percy Jackson and the Olympians</i>, or just the latter, you <b>know</b> you have to read this. What better way to learn about that adorable, <u>dysfuctional</u> family based on <b>incest</b> and gods know what else than by having its wonderful descendant pointing out to you the <i>bad</i>, the <i>
  <b>worse</b>
</i> and the <i>
  <b>
    <u>worst</u>
  </b>
</i> about this lovely and tight-knitted family of immortals?<br /><br />You are right. There is no better way.<br /><br />With chapter titles like:<br /><br />→ <i>The Golden Age of Cannibalism</i><br />→ <i>Demeter Turns into Grainzilla</i><br />→ <i>Ares, the Manly Man's Manly Man</i> and<br />→ <i>Hermes Goes to Juvie</i><br /><br />And scenes like:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Fine. Let's see what you've got, old lady!"<br />"Oooooo," said the crowd.<br />"What <b>I've</b> got?" Athena shot back. "The little girl from Lydia's going to show me how to weave? When I get through, this crowd's going to be using your tapestries for toiler paper!"<br />"Burn!" said the crowd.<br />"Oh, yeah?" Arachne sneered. "Must've been <b>dark</b> inside your daddy's head if you think you can weave better than me. Zeus probably swallowed your mama just to keep you from getting born and <b>embarrassing</b> yourself."<br />"Snap!" the crowd yelled.</i>
</blockquote><br />And:<br /><blockquote><i>Every so often Typhoeus would stomp on the earth, open a huge crevice, and reach inside to pull out some magma-like yolk from the inside of an egg. He'd throw fiery globs of lava all over the earth, setting fields on fire, melting cities, and write burning graffiti on the sides of mountains like</i> <b>ZEUS SUX</b> <i>and</i> <b>TYPHOEUS WUZ HERE</b>.</blockquote><br />And we can never forget Percy's daddy, the powerful and wise, Poseidon:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Hey, girl," he said, wiggling his eyebrows. "You must be the riptide, 'cause you sweep me off my feet."</i>
</blockquote><br />Let's just say that the assembly of those powerful and wise immortal gods that people used to worship, weren't working so right in the head and they're definitely more stupid than we thought and, of course, deserve those little nicknames that Percy made for them, like <b>Old Thunderbritches</b> *cough*we all know who we're talking about*cough*.<br /><br />To end this crazy review <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that I've warned you was going to be quotes to convince you to read this <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I'm just going to close it with Percy again, because I <b>fucking missed him that much</b>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>We've covered most of the major players. You probably know enough now to avoid getting zapped into a pile of ash if you ever come across any of the twelve Olympians.<br />Probably.<br />Me, I'm late to meet my girlfriend. Annabeth is going to kill me.<br />Hope you enjoyed the stories. <b>Stay safe out there, demigods.</b></i>
</blockquote><br />P.S. If you ever get any nightmares, remember to smack your fist on the floor and yell, <b>"Hades, tell your stupid daimons to knock it off!"</b>. It's probably their fault.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3267100386403503360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I wish all my text books were written in this way. </span>

  <span id="freeText15484907377499228431" style="display:none">I have been taken to a whole new level of story-telling. This book hits two birds with one stone by being both educational and entertaining. A very impressive publication, Uncle Rick!<br /><br />Also... Yay! Percy! A relief after The Blood of Olympus. I started this adventure with mostly Percy, and I'm so glad to be ending it with him, too.</span>

<div id="review_747706550" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/747706550" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/747706550?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer747706550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10378003491395242593">The major Greek gods, as described by Percy Jackson. Sounded good to me! I expected Percy's trademark snark, and I got plenty of that. I didn't expect it to be so detailed. I probably should have. I've never known Riordan to skimp on the research. I guess I just didn't realize how big this book would be: 300+ pages in a large-scale book. Sure, it's illustrated, but not heavily. I'm surprised to note that this is one of the most informative books of Greek myths I've ever read. Obviously, Annabeth</span>
  <span id="freeText10378003491395242593" style="display:none">The major Greek gods, as described by Percy Jackson. Sounded good to me! I expected Percy's trademark snark, and I got plenty of that. I didn't expect it to be so detailed. I probably should have. I've never known Riordan to skimp on the research. I guess I just didn't realize how big this book would be: 300+ pages in a large-scale book. Sure, it's illustrated, but not heavily. I'm surprised to note that this is one of the most informative books of Greek myths I've ever read. Obviously, Annabeth has been tutoring Percy. I would have liked this book just for the myths, but Percy's voice made me love it. Especially with his total lack of reverence for the gods, which makes the seemingly endless stories of their misbehavior easier to get through. Because 300+ pages of what terrible people the gods are could eventually be quite a slog. At any rate, this is both fun to read and packed with information. I remember reading something Riordan said about wanting this book to be useable as a study guide. Mission accomplished.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10378003491395242593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1687522497" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1687522497" />
    <a title="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20310470-pranta-ghosh-dastider"><img alt="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432710694p2/20310470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1687522497?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pranta Ghosh Dastider" href="/user/show/20310470-pranta-ghosh-dastider">Pranta Ghosh Dastider</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/22888006-percy-jackson-and-the-greek-gods">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1687522497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11102585831429768109">You know my buddy <b>Percy Jackson</b>, right? If you don't, then a big <b>WHAT</b> for you. Go and know him already. <br/><br/>You might not know me. I am but a human friend of Percy. My name is <b>Jersey Faction</b>. I live in Boston. Happy with my mom and dad (<i>they are both human btw! No gods were involved in the conspiracy of bringing me to Earth. Lucky me!</i>) . I don't go to school (<i>I just read at home. No curriculum studies or such bullshit, only fiction. Hey! don't complain. I am a fiction myself, so I am allowed to be a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11102585831429768109" style="display:none">You know my buddy <b>Percy Jackson</b>, right? If you don't, then a big <b>WHAT</b> for you. Go and know him already. <br /><br />You might not know me. I am but a human friend of Percy. My name is <b>Jersey Faction</b>. I live in Boston. Happy with my mom and dad (<i>they are both human btw! No gods were involved in the conspiracy of bringing me to Earth. Lucky me!</i>) . I don't go to school (<i>I just read at home. No curriculum studies or such bullshit, only fiction. Hey! don't complain. I am a fiction myself, so I am allowed to be anyone.</i>)<br /><br />So a few days ago I heard that Percy wrote a book. It's about the awesomeness of the Greek Gods. I was totally interested (<i>who isn't about such a piece of hard work</i>). I nagged Percy for a free copy, but he refused, and told me to buy his sweat and blood with my own money. And I did so. I guess gods wouldn't have appreciated if I had grabbed them for free. <br /><br />I read, read and read, and found out Percy literally took his life at hand when he tried to write this. That guy has courage, I tell you. See, <b>Chaos</b> and <b>Ouranos</b> were powerful enough to destroy anything (<i>including Percy</i>). My buddy told dark secrets about many of his uncle aunts and every other twisted guys and dudes that came in view. Oh and don't forget his sarcasm. Percy is a master at that. He is the most sarcastically funniest over the world topmost cool narrative guy I have ever known! Rick Riordan (<i><b>*cough cough*</b> who is not someone very important btw</i>) created him quite well (<i>I wish he had created me too, but well, I was brought to this world by a no name good for nothing all high and might stupid wannabee author</i>) in that sense. <br /><br />To be simple, I was in awe with many of their relations. Specially <b>Zeus</b> dude turned out to be a hyper active lady chaser. Hermes ran quite fast and his birthday adventure was ingenious. Liked Goddess <b>Hestia</b>. I think she is the best of them all (<i>very humble, kind of my type!</i>) I felt sorry for <b>Persephone, Hades</b>. <b>Hera</b> was the jealous kind (<i>come on lady, take care of your husband instead of punishing every other girl</i>). <b>Artemis</b> could totally be my soulmate (<i>Dear goddess please don't kill me for wishing that.</i>). <b>Poseidon</b> had some anger management issue (<i>Percy, forgive me, your dad was a Jerk, he shouldn't have done that to Athena or her followers</i>). <b>Athena</b> had some issues too, but I liked her blessings and fights. <b>Kronos</b> was a badass stupid letdown. Seriously, why eat when you have to eat that! <b>Gaia</b> did all she could and slept most of the time( and my mom shouts at me for sleeping until 9 am! She should totally read this book. ). And I seriously wish someone gave more punishment to <b>Aphrodite</b> and <b>Ares</b>, these lovebirds broke all the laws of ethics. Felt really sorry for <b>Demeter</b>, all she wanted to be humble, but she always got forced (<i>shame on you Zeus and Poseidon</i>). Oh the birth variations gods applied can never be rivaled by mankind, remember that. <br /><br />Finally, thanks buddy. I never thought mythology could be this fun. You made it possible. The modern perspectives and examples you threw in storytelling were phenomenal. I know you already are a great author. Since you already published a piece about Greek heroes I know that publishers still stands on your support. Oh! and thanks for <b>the autograph</b> at the end of the book. <br /><br />People, go read it. It's going to be the best over the multiverse twisted story you have ever read. Believe me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11102585831429768109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yHkQERSp31BkMuZ6D3yIvBpUEsoTGyYN4RD8aCvvvIzyX3nDr/cWOMMZUhv4iYJjzAv1At2WqGq6brrZ5qxOFg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
